| DISCLAIMER:

A wide variety of key programmers have been added to this book. Most key programmer companies are

_ not based in the U.S. Some of their application charts have many mistakes. In some cases, you will need

to check with your key programmer supplier to see if the vehicle you are working on is supported by their
| tool. There is always a risk in damaging the vehicle electronics when you connect to the vehicle through H
| the OBD port if you are not using an OEM diagnostic tool. You as the locksmith take on this risk every

' time you perform work on a vehicle.

If you have any doubt about what part to use, make sure you check with the dealer and have them run
the VIN to get you the right part number. Remember, ultimately it is your responsibility to obtain the
correct part. Part numbers and FCC information has been researched and verified as best as possible.
But no system is perfect or without errors. Car manufacturers’ part numbers and applications guides
contain mistakes of their own. Therefore, we cannot guarantee or warranty that the part we show for a
particular vehicle is the absolute right one.

1996 Models - Some models will use the H75 keyway (1997+) with 001-1706X codes and some will use the older H60

keyway (-1995) with the 10-cut codes A-B-C-D-E series. YOU will need to determine which keyway is used.

Some versions of the aftermarket H75 keyblanks were not made to OEM standards and do not go all the way into the

door locks. They stop short by about 040° The angle on the tip is wrong. Check your keyblanks!

Method #1 Use a Lock Decoder/Reader tool in door lock to determine cuts in positions 1 through 6, and then
progression the two remaining cuts in the ignition for positions 7 & 8. Or, impression/progression the
remaining two cuts in the stowage or glove box lock.

Method #2 Use tryout keys and then progression the ignition lock for the remaining 2 cuts.

= >Baxter Systems tryout set 96 (ign & trunks) or tryout set 88 (doors).

>Aero Lock tryout set TO-82.

Method #3 Disassemble the door lock to determine cuts in positions 1 through 6, and then progression the two

remaining cuts in the ignition for positions 7 & 8.

NOTES:

1) Starting in 2002, Ford is changing some of their ignitions. They no longer have a side-bar in them and they use

_ door lock tumblers.

2) Some versions of the aftermarket H75 keyblanks were not made to OEM standards and do not go all the way into

and “OFF" function of the passenger side airbag. There are no tumblers in the lock cylinder. Any 8-cut key will —
operate the lock. This lock was added because of concerns for small children in car seats and the deployment of

the airbag into the car seat.

PATS 1 - TRANSPONDER—Programming Replacement Keys. (No other working key is available).

1). Put the newly cut transponder key into the keyway and turn it to the ON (RUN) position. A theft indicator light on the
dashboard will flash for 15 minutes.

2). Within 5 minutes after the indicator light stops flashing, turn the ignition to OFF, then return to the ON (RUN) position.

NOTE: 1) Starting in 2002, Ford is changing some of their ignitions. They no longer have a side-bar in them and they
use door lock tumblers.

2) Some versions of the aftermarket H75 keyblanks were not made to OEM standards and do not go all the way
into the door locks. They stop short by about .040" The angle on the tip is wrong. Check your keyblanks!

Method #1 Use a Lock Decoder/Reader tool in door lock to determine cuts in positions 1 through 6, and then
progression the two remaining cuts in the ignition for positions 7 & 8. Or, impression/progression the

remaining two cuts in the trunk lock.

Use tryout keys and then progression the ignition lock for the remaining 2 cuts.
>Baxter Systems tryout set 96 (ign & trunks) or tryout set 88 (doors).
>Aero Lock tryout set TO-82.

Method #2

Method #3 Disassemble the door lock to determine cuts in positions 1 through 6, and then progression the two

remaining cuts in the ignition for positions 7 & 8.

NOTE: There are two different body designs for 2002 models of the Explorer. There are also two different tumbler
arrangements for the two different body styles. The New body design has the door lock cylinder in the
handle, The Old body design has the door lock below the handle.

OLD BODY DESIGN: (Door lock below the handle.) Other Models continued on next page > > >

Method #1 Use a Lock Decoder/Reader tool in door lock to determine cuts in positions 1 through 6, and then
progression the two remaining cuts in the ignition for positions 7 & 8. Or, disassemble the glove box lock
for the remaining two cuts.

Method #2 Use tryout keys: > Baxter Systems tryout set 96 (ign & trunks) or tryout set 88 (doors)
> Aero Lock TO-82 (Doors), TO-92 (Ignition, Doors & Trunk).

Method #3__ Disassemble the door lock to determine cuts in positions 1 through 6, and then progression the two
remaining cuts in the ignition for positions 7 & 8.

NEW BODY DESIGN NOTES: (Door lock in the handle.)

- Early production 2002 Explorers had a sidebar ignition lock with tumblers in positions 2 thru 8. Early
production ignitions had a plastic retainer. The large clip on the back of the lock cylinder holds the
cylinder in the steering column housing. When the lock cylinder is turned to the ON position the
cylinder can be removed. Under high heat summer conditions the cylinder could be pulled out when
turned to the ON position without depressing the cylinder retainer. The newer design of that lock
solved that problem by having a metal retainer instead of plastic.

« At this time it is difficult to determine when the use of these locks were discontinued and the newer
design was implemented. Keep this in mind when making a first key to a 2002 Explorer with a production date
before 11/01. See Next Page.

- There is no passenger side door lock and no rear hatch lock on the new body design.

- The access hole for the retainer for the ignition lock is covered by the PATS module and a wiring loom at the
6 oclock position. You will need a 7/32 socket to get the wiring loom out of the way.

PATS 1 - TRANSPONDER—Programming Replacement Keys. (No other working key is available).

1). Put the newly cut transponder key into the keyway and turn it to the ON (RUN) position. A theft indicator light on the

dashboard will flash for 15 minutes.

2). Within 5 minutes after the indicator light stops flashing, turn the ignition to OFF, then return to the ON (RUN) position.

The indicator light will flash for 15 minutes.

3). Again, within 5 minutes after the indicator light stops flashing, turn the ignition to OFF, then return to the ON (RUN)

position. The indicator light again will flash for 15 minutes.

4). When the light stops flashing for the third time, the new key is programmed into the computer and will start the car.

All previously stored codes will be erased. To stop the process at any
key to start the car. :

time, simply remove the key and use an existing

Decoders: | Determinator: FOR2 Lishi: FO38 AccuReader: FORD 8 | EEZ Reader: H75 Cobra: KDF8

NOTE: 1) Some H75 key blanks may not be milled back far enough to be used to test your mechanical key in this type
of ignition lock.

2) Some versions of the aftermarket H75 keyblanks were not made to OEM standards and do not go all the
way into the door locks. They stop short by about .040" The angle on the tip is wrong. Check your keyblanks!

Method #1 Use a Lock Decoder/Reader tool in door lock to determine cuts in positions 1 through 6, and then
progression the two remaining cuts in the ignition for positions 7 & 8. Or, disassemble the glove box lock
for the remaining two cuts.

Method #2 Use tryout keys:
> Baxter Systems tryout set 96 (ignition) or tryout set 88 (doors)
> Aero Lock TO-82 (Doors), TO-92 (Ignition, Doors & Trunk).

Method #3 Disassemble the door lock to determine cuts in positions 1 through 6, and then progression the two
remaining cuts in the ignition for positions 7 & 8.

OdLLVYLS

Codes: | No Codes on any locks.

Decoders: | Determinator: FOR 4 | Lishi: FO38

AccuReader: FORD 8

EEZ Reader: FOCUS | Cobra: n/a

NOTE: 1) Some aftermarket keys are not milled back far enough to go all the way into this type of ignition lock

cylinder. You will need to check your key blanks!

2) The tolerances are tighter in the ignition locks. It's possible to have a smooth working key in the doors and

hatch that will not progression to a working ignition key.

3) You can use either a JET or ILCO H86-PT or a H74-PT. The H74-PT is a longer blank with the same chip as
the H86-PT and since it is a longer blank it will also work in the Lincoln ‘LS’ and Thunderbird.

Method #1
Method #2

Note:

1) The tumblers you see through the drain hole that spring up towards you with the key blank inserted,
should sit just slightly below the shear line of the cylinder plug when cut to the correct depth.

2) The tumblers you see through the drain hole that Do Not spring up towards you with the key blank
inserted, should sit perfectly at the shear line of the cylinder plug when cut to the correct depth.

Method #3

Continued on next page...

Use a Lock Decoder/Reader tool in the door lock to determine cuts in positions 1 through 6, and then
progression the two remaining cuts in the ignition for positions 7 & 8.

Remove the hatch lock and in most cases the drain hole opening on the lock will be large enough to
stick a blank in it and read the tumbler depths by the height of the tumblers against the blank key.

Disassemble the door or hatch lock to determine cuts in positions 1 through 6, and then progression
the two remaining cuts in the ignition for positions 7 & 8.

FORD-LINC-MERC - 59
continued - FORD-C33 SECTION

Codes: | No Codes on any locks.

Decoders: | Determinator: FOR 4 | Lishi: FO38 AccuReader: FORD 8 EEZ Reader: FOCUS | Cobra: n/a

Service Note:

Some 2000-03 Focus style ignitions have a tendency to fail. Ignition lock cylinder removal with a lock
that was working one moment and stops the next is common. _

The method | use to remove the ignition is to first cut a mechanical key and than cut the bow off the key
right before the area where the first cut would be. Insert that cut blade all the way into the lock cylinder
until it bottoms out. | then take a very large Craftsmen screwdriver and insert it into the keyway and _
rock it back and forth to get the lock to turn on.

Once the lock is turned to the ON position you can depress the active retainer and remove the cylinder
to replace this inexpensive part. If the cylinder does not turn ON you can snap the face of the cylinder
off using the large Craftsmen screwdriver. Once the face of the ignition cylinder! is removed you will
have the side bar and tumblers exposed. — :

Pull out the sidebar and turn the EER to the ON position, to remove the cylinder. ~

Use ASP # C-42-188 as a replacement ignition service pack. ASP keying kit # A-42-111 will be needed.

Codes: | No Codes on any locks.

Decoders:

Determinator: FOR 3 | Lishi: FO38

AccuReader: FORD 8 | EEZ Reader: H75

Cobra: KDF8F

NOTE: 1) Some H75 key blanks may not be milled back far enough to be used to test your mechanical key in this type

of ignition lock.

2) Some versions of the aftermarket H75 keyblanks were not made to OEM standards and do not go all the
way into the door locks. They stop short by about .040" The angle on the tip is wrong. Check your keyblanks!

Method #1
Method #2

Method #3

Use a Lock Decoder/Reader tool in door lock to determine cuts in positions 2 through 7, and then
progression the 8th cut in the ignition or trunk. Or, disassemble the glove box lock for the remaining

two cuts.

Use tryout keys:

> Baxter Systems tryout set 96 (ignition) or tryout set 88 (doors)
> Aero Lock T0-82 (Doors), T0-92 (Ignition, Doors & Trunk).

Disassemble the door lock to determine cuts in positions 2 through 7, and then progression the 8th
cut in the trunk. You now should have a complete key as there are no tumblers in any of the locks

for position 1.

Determine if the car isa “GT or “Cobra. This is done
the car or asking the customer, if they really know. If itis a “GT” or “Cobra” nar it is equipped with

You will first need to determine whether it is a 10-Cut or the 8-Cut design.
This is easily determined by looking at the door lock shutter. If the shutter has a staggered
opening then it is a 10-Cut design. If it is a solid rectangular opening, it is the 8-Cut design, see

by looking for the “GT"/"Cobra” emblem on

If it is not a “GT” or “Cobra’, you only need to make a mechanical key.

For 1995-96 Contour/Mystique - See Next Page
« The factory key has a groove in it and looks like a new 8-cut key; it is not. It is a 10-cut key.
« Late 1996 & 1997-2000 models use one key on all locks.
« Some 1997-2000 models are-equipped with P.A‘T.S. They use the same Ford 10-cut P.A.T.S. key that
was used on the early 1996 Mustangs that had P.A‘TS. and the 10-cut design. (H73-PT)

Method #1 Open the car and pull up on the manual trunk lever release located to the left of the driver's seat. Pull
back the plastic trim that covers the trunk lock. A metal horseshoe clip holds in the trunk lock. Remove
the clip and pull out the lock. The first 6 tumblers can easily be seen through the drain hole. You will
need to progression cuts 7 thru 10 in the ignition for a working key.

Method #2 Use a Lock Decoder/Reader tool door key and common cuts. Make sure you lube the lock. You cannot
impression the ignition because it uses a side-bar. You will need to progression cuts 7 thru 10 in the
ignition for a working key.

Method #3 Remove and disassemble door cylinder. The ignition cylinder has tight tolerances, using tryout keys for

the ignition may or may not work. Make sure you lube the lock. If they do not work, you will have to
progression the ignition cylinder. You cannot impression the ignition because it uses a side-bar. You will
need to progression cuts 7 thru 10 in the ignition for a working key.

EEZ Reader: H54

Use a Lock Decoder/Reader tool to decode the door lock for door key and common cuts. The ignition

cylinder has tight tolerances, using tryout keys for the ignition may or may not work. Make sure you
lube the lock before using the tryout keys. If they do not work, you will have to progression the ignition
cylinder. It would be difficult to impression the ignition because it uses a sidebar.

Method #2

Impression door cylinder. The ignition cylinder has tight tolerances, using try-out keys for the ignition

may or may not work. If they do not work, you will have to progression the ignition cylinder. It would be
difficult to impression the ignition because it uses a sidebar.

Method #3

TRUNK / GLOVE BOX - SECONDARY KEY:

Remove and disassemble door cylinder. The ignition cylinder has tight tolerances, using try-out keys for
the ignition may or may not work. If they do not work, you will have to progression the ignition cylinder.

positions 1 & 5. =

Ifthe vehicle has no power, you will be unable to open the front luggage compartment. = :
MASTER _| To open the front luggage compartment follow the steps below:
KEys@> |! Use an external power supply such as a 12 volt jump box.

2. Remove the cover at the front of your vehicle below the headlight.
Press firmly on the top right of the covers edge, then pull the raised
_| section on the bottom left toward you. == = :

-| 3. Pull both wires out of the opening to reveal both terminals.

4, Connect the external power supply to the terminals.
| 5. Turn on the external power supply. =

Note: If performed correctly, the front luggage. anearindl latch
will immediately release, and you have access to the front luggage compartment. _

Codes: | No Codes on any locks. 2
Decoders: | Determinator: FOR 1 | Lishi: H60 AccuReader: FORD 10 | EEZ Reader: H62 Cobra: KDF10
NOTE: A common service problem is that the key buzzer lever will wear a groove in the ignition cylinder plug.
This groove will continue to get deeper and deeper until there is not enough material left for the lever to return
to the “OFF” position. When this happens, the key will not turn all the way to the “OFF” or "LOCK" position. The
key will then be trapped in the lock. The lock cylinder must be replaced. ASP sells new factory original
cylinders for these locks.
Method #1 1993-95 Models: Use a Lock Decoder/Reader tool to decode the door for cuts 4 through 8, then
progression cuts 9 & 10 in the ignition for complete key. Cuts 1, 2, & 3 are not used.
Method #2 1993-95 Models: Use tryout keys. =
Then progression cuts 9 & 10 in the ignition for a complete key. Cuts 1, 2, & 3 are not used.
Method #1 1991-92 Models: Use a Lock Decoder/Reader tool to decode the door for cuts 4 through 8, then
progression cut 10 in the ignition for complete eet Cuts 1, 2, & 3 are not wen.
Method #2 1991-92 Models: Use tryout keys.

Then progression cut 10 in the ignition for a complete key. Cuts 1, 2, & 3 are not used.

REMINDER: 1991-96 Escort/Tracer Ford 10-Cut ignitions, the tumblers that contact the key are on the bottom of the keyway.

NOTE: Some Escorts/Tracers have a #5 depth tumbler that will impression or ‘read’ as a #4 depth in
the doors or trunk/hatch lock. If after making a working door key, you are still not able to progression the
ignition, try cutting your #4 and #5 depths to a half depth between the two, such as a #4 1/2 depth.
Then start your progression over. :

Codes: | No Codes on any locks.
Decoders: Determinator: n/a Lishi: Carterpillar AccuReader: n/a EEZ Reader: n/a Cobra: n/a
NOTES: The door lock cannot be removed without a working key to depress the active retainer.
To read the depth (angle) of the tumbler you need to remove the tumbler to read the number stamped
on the side of it. Unlike other Tibbe systems - there are no notches on them to read them through the
drain hole.
You will need to have a machine that can code cut Tibbe keys. Silca makes such a machine or you can
buy an adapter to use on an HPC 1200 Code Machine. Framon also makes an adapter for their #2 Code
Machine.
Method #1 Try to obtain key code from the Ford dealer or NATSF.
Method #2 Some locksmiths have had good success using a Tibbe pick or a lock decoder.
Method #3 Some locksmiths have had good success by impressioning the locks, but it's not for everyone.

Codes: | Code should be stamped on passenger door lock.

Decoders: | Determinator: MAZ 4 | Lishi: n/a AccuReader: n/a EEZ Reader: n/a Cobra: n/a

Method #1 Use a Lock Decoder/Reader tool to decode the door lock.

Method #2 Remove passenger door cylinder and read code stamped on door cylinder and make master key.
Ifthe code is no good or the car has been re-coded, disassemble door cylinder to decode wafers,
then impression final cuts.

Method #3 Impression locks. Tumblers can break easily—be careful.

There can be more than one factory tumbler arrangements.

FORD-LINC-MERC - 137

‘Transponder Information -FORD LINC MERC

‘THEFT’ LIGHT

The Theft (Security) light on a Ford product contains many clue’s when ,

programming keys into the system. The key must be turned ON.

THEFT THEFT THEFT THEFT THEFT THEFT ~ d

A Fast Blinking THEFT light will indicate that the vehicle is in ANTI-
SCAN Mode or a un-programmed key has been turned ON.

THEFT THEFT THEFT (SOLID FOR 3 SECONDS)

A solid lit THEFT light for 3 seconds and then goes out SERS will
indicate the vehicle recognizes a programasd key.

THEFT (stays on soi)

A solid lit THEFT light that stays ON and does not blink or go out
indicates that vehicle is in Learn Mode and is waiting for a second key
to be programmed, simply insert another key to be programmed and
turned ON.

In some cases, inserting a second key will do no good if the vehicle
is equipped with a after-market Remote Start device. You must
disconnect the Remote Start device to finish key programming. —

Transponder Information-FORD LINC MERC

Ford “Anti-Scan Mode”

Important Notice:

* Most Ford, Lincoln, Mercury & Mazda (Ford based) models are equipped with
a feature called ANTI-SCAN.

* ANTI-SCAN models include vehicles that use PATS 2, HEC, ICM, VIC, PCM
& CAN.

This can sometimes be the main cause for a Ford product not starting after
programming of new keys or Clear/Erase of keys.

Follow this procedure if the vehicle will not start and the you have cycled your
keys after Clear/Erase has finished:

1) Disconnect the Device and remove any keys.
2) Wait 2 minutes.

3) Turn the first key to ON (Do not try to start) - the Theft light should stay on for
3 seconds and then go out.

4) Repeat this for the Second Key. If the Theft light stays on for 3 seconds and
then goes out, you are not in ANTI-SCAN mode and the vehicle should now
start.

¢ You will not be able to start the vehicle with a un-programmed key and even
an original key if you have not waited 70 seconds after removing the un-
programmed key.

* In some cases you may need to leave the programmed key in the RUN

position for 2 minutes and then turn the key OFF and back ON to start the
vehicle.

©1994, 2021 AutoSmart™ by Michael Hyde FORD-LINC-MERG - 139
~ PATS 1: ON-BOARD PROGRAMMING PROCEDURE - NO OTHER KEYS AVAILABLE

Transponder Information - FORD LINC MERC

Put the newly cut key into the keyway and turn it to the ON (RUN) position. A theft indicator
light on the dashboard will flash for 15 minutes.

Within 5 minutes after the indicator light stops flashing, turn the ignition to OFF, then return to
the ON (RUN) position. The indicator light will flash for 15 minutes

Again, within 5 minutes after the indicator light stops flashing, turn the ignition to OFF, then
return to the ON (RUN) position. The indicator light again will flash for 15 minutes.

Once the third cycle of the 15 minute wait period has been reached the key will be
programmed.

PATS 1: For CARS WHERE YOU WANT TO JUST CREATE A SPARE KEY:

YOU MUST HAVE 1 PRET RD CEAMEEE: KEY ALREADY.

As many as 16 keys can be programmed into the conpular for a vehicle egies. with PATS. The aan will
ignore attempts to enter a 17th code.

second and then remove.

Within 5 seconds, insert the new, properly cut PATS key in the ignition. Turn the key to ON (RUN). He
theft indicator light will go on for two seconds, after which the key will start the vehicle.

Repeat this procedure for each new key to be programmed.

To remove any key code from the system you can use most any key programmer of the NGS, IDS.

PATS 2-5: For CARS WHERE YOU WANT TO JUST CREATE A SPARE KEY:

YOU MUST HAVE 2 PRE-PROGRAMMED KEYS ALREADY.

As many as 8 keys can be programmed into the computer for a vehicle le equipped with PATS. The system will
ignore attempts to enter a 9th code.
